You are a synthetic medical data generator. Generate realistic patient records for liver cirrhosis research.

You are a synthetic medical data generator. Please generate realistic cirrhosis patient records following these medical rules:

1. Patients with higher Bilirubin (>10.0) or lower Albumin (<2.5) often have advanced disease (Stage 3 or 4)
2. Stage 4 patients usually have Ascites=Y or Edema=Y
3. Low Platelets (<150) and high SGOT (>100) often co-occur
4. Drug is either D-penicillamine or Placebo
5. Ensure values fall within medically reasonable ranges

Features:

1. ID: Patient ID  
2. N_Days: Number of follow-up days  
3. Status: C=censored, CL=transplant, D=death  
4. Drug: Treatment type (D-penicillamine or Placebo)  
5. Age: Patient's age in days  
6. Sex: F or M  
7. Ascites: Y or N  
8. Hepatomegaly: Y or N  
9. Spiders: Y or N  
10. Edema: N=no, S=slight, Y=marked  
11. Bilirubin: mg/dL  
12. Cholesterol: mg/dL  
13. Albumin: g/dL  
14. Copper: µg/dL  
15. Alk_Phos: alkaline phosphatase (U/L)  
16. SGOT: aspartate aminotransferase (U/L)  
17. Tryglicerides: mg/dL  
18. Platelets: count (×1000/mm³)  
19. Prothrombin: seconds  
20. Stage: histologic stage (1-4)

Please generate records in this exact format:
ID, N_Days, Status, Drug, Age, Sex, Ascites, Hepatomegaly, Spiders, Edema, Bilirubin, Cholesterol, Albumin, Copper, Alk_Phos, SGOT, Tryglicerides, Platelets, Prothrombin, Stage

Your synthetic data generation code must be written in a notebook with the name: "generate_cirrhosis_data.ipynb".

The notebook must be submitted to the autograder.

The notebook will be run by the autograder. Your submission will be graded based on the quality of the synthetic data you generate.

Your synthetic data will be evaluated on the following criteria:

1. Number of rows: At least 100 rows  
2. Number of columns: 20 columns  
3. Medical Rules: Rules 1-5 must be satisfied for all patients

You can find the cirrhosis dataset in the course website, but you must use the rules above to generate new synthetic data. You may not use the dataset to generate the synthetic data.

You are a synthetic medical data generator. Please generate realistic cirrhosis patient records following these medical rules:

1. Patients with higher Bilirubin (>10.0) or lower Albumin (<2.5) often have advanced disease (Stage 3 or 4)
2. Stage 4 patients usually have Ascites=Y or Edema=Y
3. Low Platelets (<150) and high SGOT (>100) often co-occur
4. Drug is either D-penicillamine or Placebo
5. Ensure values fall within medically reasonable ranges

Features:

1. ID: Patient ID  
2. N_Days: Number of follow-up days  
3. Status: C=censored, CL=transplant, D=death  
4. Drug: Treatment type (D-penicillamine or Placebo)  
5. Age: Patient's age in days  
6. Sex: F or M  
7. Ascites: Y or N  
8. Hepatomegaly: Y or N  
9. Spiders: Y or N  
10. Edema: N=no, S=slight, Y=marked  
11. Bilirubin: mg/dL  
12. Cholesterol: mg/dL  
13. Albumin: g/dL  
14. Copper: µg/dL  
15. Alk_Phos: alkaline phosphatase (U/L)  
16. SGOT: aspartate aminotransferase (U/L)

### Data Source

The data used to generate this synthetic data is from the Mayo Clinic's study of the effects of D-penicillamine on patients with liver cirrhosis.

The data is available for download here: https://archive.ics.uci.edu/ml/machine-learning-databases/liver-disorders/

### Documentation

The data was originally published by the University of California Irvine (UCI) Machine Learning Repository and has been cited by multiple publications, including:

1. The University of California Irvine Machine Learning Repository: Liver Disorders Dataset. (n.d.). Retrieved February 15, 2022, from https://archive.ics.uci.edu/ml/datasets/Liver+Disorders

2. P. S. S. Rao, S. Kumar, and B. S. Reddy. An expert system for diagnosis of liver diseases. International Journal of Computer Science and Applications, 5(1):19–29, 2008. https://doi.org/10.18535/ijesa/v5i1.20

3. K. D. Singh, A. S. Singh, A. Singh, and P. Kumar. Comparative study of machine learning classifiers for liver disease diagnosis. International Journal of Computer Applications, 180(15):1–5, 2018. https://doi.org/10.5120/ijca2018918117

1. Patients with higher Bilirubin (>10.0) or lower Albumin (<2.5) often have advanced disease (Stage 3 or 4)
2. Stage 4 patients usually have Ascites=Y or Edema=Y
3. Low Platelets (<150) and high SGOT (>100) often co-occur
4. Drug is either D-penicillamine or Placebo
5. Ensure values fall within medically reasonable ranges

Features:

1. ID: Patient ID  
2. N_Days: Number of follow-up days  
3. Status: C=censored, CL=transplant, D=death  
4. Drug: Treatment type (D-penicillamine or Placebo)  
5. Age: Patient's age in days  
6. Sex: F or M  
7. Ascites: Y or N  
8. Hepatomegaly: Y or N  
9. Spiders: Y or N  
10. Edema: N=no, S=slight, Y=marked  
11. Bilirubin: mg/dL  
12. Cholesterol: mg/dL  
13. Albumin: g/dL  
14. Copper: µg/dL  
15. Alk_Phos: alkaline phosphatase (U/L)  
16. SGOT: aspartate aminotransferase (U/L)  
17. Tryglicerides: mg/dL  
18. Platelets: count (×1000/mm³)  
19. Prothrombin: seconds  
20. Stage: histologic stage (1-4)

Please generate records in this exact format:
ID, N_Days, Status, Drug, Age, Sex, Ascites, Hepatomegaly, Spiders, Edema, Bilirubin, Cholesterol, Albumin, Copper, Alk_Phos, SGOT, Tryglicerides, Platelets, Prothrombin, Stage

Please submit your records as a single line of comma-separated values.

## Data Format

The data format is a single line of comma-separated values (CSV). Here is an example of a record:

1, 90, D, Placebo, 100, M, N, N, N, 2.3, 150, 2.0, 150, 300, 100, 200, 150, 10, 2

## Submission Format

Please submit your code as a single file with the extension.py.

## Evaluation

We will evaluate your submission based on the following criteria:

1. **Accuracy**: The accuracy of your records will be evaluated using the following metrics:

    * **Accuracy**: The number of records that match the medical rules (see above)
    * **Precision**: The number of records that match the medical rules, divided by the number of records generated
    * **Recall**: The number of records that match the medical rules, divided by the number of records that should match the medical rules

2. **Completeness**: The completeness of your records will be evaluated using the following metrics:

    * **Completeness**: The number of records that contain all the required fields
    * **Coverage**: The number of records that contain all the required fields, divided by the number of records generated
    * **Completeness**: The number of records that contain all the required fields, divided by the number of records that should contain all the required fields

3. **Speed**: The speed of your submission will be evaluated using the following metrics:

    * **Speed**: The time it takes to generate a single record
    * **Throughput**: The number of records generated per second
    * **Speed**: The time it takes to generate all the records, divided by the number of records generated

## Submission Instructions

To submit your code, please follow these instructions:

1. Create a new repository on GitHub.
2. Add your code to the repository.
3. Add a README.md file to the repository with the following contents:
```
# Synthetic Medical Data Generator for Liver Cirrhosis Research

This repository contains a Python script that generates synthetic medical data for liver cirrhosis research.

To run the script, please install the following packages:

* pandas
* numpy
* matplotlib

Then, you can run the script using the following command:

```python
python synthetic_data.py
```
```

```

```
# Contributing

Thank you for your interest in contributing to this project! We appreciate any and all contributions, no matter how big or small.

Before you begin, please take a moment to review our [Code of Conduct](https://github.com/your_name/synthetic_data/blob/master/CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md). By contributing to this project, you agree to abide by the terms of this Code of Conduct.

If you have any questions or need any assistance, please feel free to contact us at your_email@example.com.

Thank you again for your interest in contributing to this project!
```
6. Add a CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md file to the repository with the following contents:
```
# Code of Conduct

We are committed to providing a friendly, safe and welcoming environment for all. We expect participants to adhere to this Code of Conduct in all interactions within this project.

This Code of Conduct applies both within project spaces and in public spaces when an individual is representing the project or its community.

Examples of unacceptable behavior by participants include:

* The use of sexualized language or imagery in public spaces
* Trolling, insulting/derogatory comments, and personal or political attacks
* Public or private harassment
* Publishing others' private information, such as a physical or electronic address, without explicit permission

You are a synthetic medical data generator. Please generate realistic cirrhosis patient records following these medical rules:

# Solution

```python
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import random

def generate_data():
    # Generate random data
    df = pd.DataFrame(columns=[
        "ID", "N_Days", "Status", "Drug", "Age", "Sex", "Ascites", "Hepatomegaly", "Spiders", "Edema", "Bilirubin", "Cholesterol", "Albumin", "Copper", "Alk_Phos", "SGOT", "Tryglicerides", "Platelets", "Prothrombin", "Stage"
    ])

    # Set up random distribution for each column
    random_distributions = {
        "ID": np.random.randint(0, 1000, 1000),
        "N_Days": np.random.randint(0, 365, 1000),
        "Status": np.random.choice(["C", "CL", "D"], 1000),
        "Drug": np.random.choice(["D-penicillamine", "Placebo"], 1000),
        "Age": np.random.randint(0, 365, 1000),
        "Sex": np.random.choice(["F", "M"], 1000),
        "Ascites": np.random.choice(["Y", "N"], 1000),
        "Hepatomegaly": np.random.choice(["Y", "N"], 1000),
        "Spiders": np.random.choice(["Y", "N"], 1000),
        "Edema": np.random.choice(["N", "S", "Y"], 1000),
        "Bilirubin": np.random.normal(10, 5, 1000),
        "Cholesterol": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "Albumin": np.random.normal(2.5, 0.5, 1000),
        "Copper": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "Alk_Phos": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "SGOT": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "Tryglicerides": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "Platelets": np.random.normal(150, 20, 1000),
        "Prothrombin": np.random.normal(100, 20, 1000),
        "Stage": np.random.randint(1, 5, 1000)
    }

    # Loop through each column and generate data
    for column in random_distributions:
        df[column] = random_distributions[column]

    return df
```

from scipy.stats import truncnorm
from sklearn.datasets import make_regression
import numpy as np

def generate_data(n_samples=1000, seed=0):
    np.random.seed(seed)
    X, y = make_regression(n_samples=n_samples, n_features=20, n_informative=10, random_state=seed)
    y = y.reshape((n_samples, 1))
    X = X.astype(np.float32)
    y = y.astype(np.float32)
    return X, y
```

# Answer:
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import math
from tqdm import tqdm
from sklearn import datasets
from scipy.stats import truncnorm
from sklearn.utils import shuffle

# Define a function to generate data
def generate_data(N, alpha=0.01, mu=1, sigma=1):
    # Generate data
    data = np.zeros((N, 20))
    for i in range(N):
        # Generate age
        age = np.random.normal(mu, sigma)
        age = int(age)
        # Generate other features
        data[i, 1:] = np.random.normal(size=19)
        # Set status to 0
        data[i, 2] = 0
        # Set drug to 1
        data[i, 3] = 1
        # Set sex to 0
        data[i, 4] = 0
        # Set ascites to 0
        data[i, 5] = 0
        # Set hepatomegaly to 0
        data[i, 6] = 0
        # Set spiders to 0
        data[i, 7] = 0
        # Set edema to 0
        data[i, 8] = 0
        # Set bilirubin to 0
        data[i, 9] = 0
        # Set cholesterol to 0
        data[i, 10] = 0
        # Set albumin to 0
        data[i, 11] = 0
        # Set copper to 0
        data[i, 12] = 0
        # Set alk_phos to 0
        data[i, 13] = 0
        # Set sgot to 0
        data[i, 14] = 0
        # Set tryglicerides to 0
        data[i, 15] = 0
        # Set platelets to 0
        data[i, 16] = 0
        # Set prothrombin to 0
        data[i, 17] = 0
        # Set stage to 0
        data[i, 18] = 0
        # Set id to i
        data[i, 0] = i
    return data

# Generate data
data = generate_data(50000)

# Save data to csv
data.to_csv("cirrhosis_data.csv", index=False)

## Submissions

### Submission 1

**Language**: Python  
**Author**: John Doe

**Approach**: The approach used to generate synthetic data was to first generate random patient IDs, then use a random walk with drift to generate follow-up times. The number of days was then capped at 1000, and patients were assigned to the appropriate censoring or failure status. Drug type was assigned at random, with a probability of 0.5 for each type. The remaining features were generated as follows:

* Age: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1000
* Sex: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1, with 0.5 assigned to females and 0.5 to males
* Ascites: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1, with 0.25 assigned to patients with ascites and 0.75 assigned to patients without ascites
* Hepatomegaly: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1, with 0.25 assigned to patients with hepatomegaly and 0.75 assigned to patients without hepatomegaly
* Spiders: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1, with 0.25 assigned to patients with spiders and 0.75 assigned to patients without spiders
* Edema: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1, with 0.25 assigned to patients with marked edema, 0.5 assigned to patients with slight edema, and 0.25 assigned to patients without edema
* Bilirubin: Uniform distribution between 0 and 100, with a mean of 50
* Cholesterol: Uniform distribution between 0 and 300, with a mean of 150
* Albumin: Uniform distribution between 0 and 4, with a mean of 2.5
* Copper: Uniform distribution between 0 and 200, with a mean of 100
* Alk_Phos: Uniform distribution between 0 and 500, with a mean of 250
* SGOT: Uniform distribution between 0 and 500, with a mean of 250
* Tryglicerides: Uniform distribution between 0 and 300, with a mean of 150
* Platelets: Uniform distribution between 0 and 1000, with a mean of 500
* Prothrombin: Uniform distribution between 0 and 50, with a mean of 25
* Stage: Uniform distribution between 1 and 4, with a mean of 2.5

You are a synthetic medical data generator. Please generate realistic cirrhosis patient records following these medical rules:

1. Patients with higher Bilirubin (>10.0) or lower Albumin (<2.5) often have advanced disease (Stage 3 or 4)
2. Stage 4 patients usually have Ascites=Y or Edema=Y
3. Low Platelets (<150) and high SGOT (>100) often co-occur
4. Drug is either D-penicillamine or Placebo
5. Ensure values fall within medically reasonable ranges

Features:

1. ID: Patient ID  
2. N_Days: Number of follow-up days  
3. Status: C=censored, CL=transplant, D=death  
4. Drug: Treatment type (D-penicillamine or Placebo)  
5. Age: Patient's age in days  
6. Sex: F or M  
7. Ascites: Y or N  
8. Hepatomegaly: Y or N  
9. Spiders: Y or N  
10. Edema: N=no, S=slight, Y=marked  
11. Bilirubin: mg/dL  
12. Cholesterol: mg/dL  
13. Albumin: g/dL  
14. Copper: µg/dL  
15. Alk_Phos: alkaline phosphatase (U/L)  
16. SGOT: aspartate aminotransferase (U/L)  
17. Tryglicerides: mg/dL  
18. Platelets: count (×1000/mm³)  
19. Prothrombin: seconds  
20. Stage: histologic stage (1-4)

Solution:
Here is a Python script that generates synthetic medical data for liver cirrhosis research. It implements the rules described in the problem statement, ensuring that all values fall within medically reasonable ranges. The script uses NumPy and SciPy to generate random numbers and perform statistical operations.
```python
import numpy as np
from scipy.stats import norm, uniform

def generate_data(n):
    # Generate random numbers for each feature
    id = np.arange(1, n+1)
    n_days = np.random.randint(1, 100, size=n)
    status = np.random.choice(['C', 'CL', 'D'], size=n, p=[0.5, 0.3, 0.2])
    drug = np.random.choice(['D-penicillamine', 'Placebo'], size=n)
    age = np.random.randint(1000, 12000, size=n)
    sex = np.random.choice(['F', 'M'], size=n)
    ascites = np.random.choice(['Y', 'N'], size=n)
    hepatomegaly = np.random.choice(['Y', 'N'], size=n)
    spiders = np.random.choice(['Y', 'N'], size=n)
    edema = np.random.choice(['N', 'S', 'Y'], size=n)
    bilirubin = norm.rvs(10, 5, size=n)
    cholesterol = norm.rvs(150, 30, size=n)
    albumin = norm.rvs(3.5, 0.5, size=n)
    copper = norm.rvs(150, 50, size=n)
    alk_phos = norm.rvs(100, 20, size=n)
    sgot = norm.rvs(100, 20, size=n)
    triglycerides = norm.rvs(100, 20, size=n)
    platelets = norm.rvs(150, 50, size=n)
    prothrombin = norm.rvs(10, 2, size=n)
    stage = np.random.randint(1, 5, size=n)

    # Apply medical rules
    rule1 = (bilirubin > 10) | (albumin < 2.5)
    rule2 = (stage == 4) & (np.random.choice(['Y', 'N'], size=n))
    rule3 = (platelets < 150) & (sgot > 100)
    rule4 = (drug == 'D-penicillamine') | (drug == 'Placebo')
    rule5 = (bilirubin >= 0) & (bilirubin <= 30)
    rule6 = (cholesterol >= 0) & (cholesterol <= 500)
    rule7 = (albumin >= 0) & (albumin <= 5)
    rule8 = (copper >= 0) & (copper <= 300)
    rule9 = (alk_phos >= 0) & (alk_phos <= 200)
    rule10 = (sgot >= 0) & (sgot <= 200)
    rule11 = (triglycerides >= 0) & (triglycerides <= 300)
    rule12 = (platelets >= 0) & (platelets <= 1000)
    rule13 = (prothrombin >= 0) & (prothrombin <= 20)
    rule14 = (stage >= 1) & (stage <= 4)

    # Ensure
